Drive by Press Nomadic American Printmaking - Group Show



Drive by Press is coming to Hendrix! They will have a group show of prints.
DBP is a collaborative print experience on wheels. They call themselves
=E2=80=9CMissionaries of Print=E2=80=9D as they travel the nation with thei=
r 200 pound,
14th-century-style printing press loaded up in a 21st-century vehicle. DBP
has exhibited thousands of prints nationwide, producing more than 50,000
pieces of wearable art along the way.



Show Dates: Monday, Nov.14 =E2=80=94 Tuesday, Dec. 6

Location: Art A Lobby



*ANNOUNCEMENTS*


Help Refugees: Winter Clothing Drive



Want to help refugees but don=E2=80=99t know how? The International Rescue
Committee (IRC) provides opportunities for refugees, asylees, victims of
human trafficking, survivors of torture, and other immigrants to thrive in
America. The IRC in Baltimore is seeking donations of winter clothing to
help newly arrived refugees in the Baltimore area stay warm during the cold
months. We are in need of the following items in new or good used
condition: Coats and Jackets, Winter Hats, Gloves and Scarves, or Winter
Boots.



Please drop these items in the box inside the Miller Center. All sizes for
any age group and gender are welcome. If you have any questions, please
contact Roshaneh Ali at alirr@hendrix.edu.


Documentary Film Internship Opportunity in Little Rock (Spring 2017)



*Pipeline* is a feature length documentary film about Arkansas=E2=80=99s =
=E2=80=9CCradle to
Prison Pipeline,=E2=80=9D exploring issues of childhood trauma, education, =
juvenile
detention, and mass incarceration, specifically addressing the ways they
play out on a state level. Film producer, Zachary Crow, is looking for a
spring semester intern to work 12-15 hours weekly on this Little Rock based
project. For more information, please see the job posting on HireHendrix
<http://hendrix-csm.symplicity.com/students/index.php>. Questions about the
Hendrix internship program? Stop by SLTC 2nd floor during walk-in hours
Wednesdays 1 p.m. =E2=80=94 4 p.m. and Thursdays 9 a.m. =E2=80=94 1 p.m. or=
 call
501-450-1440 to schedule an appointment.


Department of Energy Paid "Science Undergraduate Laboratory Internships"
(SULI)



The SULI program places students as paid interns in science and engineering
research activities at DOE national laboratories and facilities, working
with laboratory staff scientists and engineers on projects related to
ongoing research programs. Appointments are for 10 weeks during the summer
term, are open to US Citizens and US Lawful Permanent Residents, include a
weekly stipend, reimbursement for one round trip domestic travel to the
participant=E2=80=99s host DOE laboratory, and possibilities for a housing
allowance. More than 850 internships are sponsored annually. That's right,
850 internships!



Full program information and descriptions, including links to the online
application system, are available by click the link
<http://science.energy.gov/wdts/suli/>. Need help with your application
materials or have questions about internships? Stop by The Office of Career
Services: SLTC 2nd floor to set an appointment or stop by walk-in hours
every Wednesday from 1 p.m. =E2=80=94 4 p.m., or Thursday from 9 a.m. =E2=
=80=94 1 p.m. no
appointment necessary.

Announcing the 2017 African American History Month Reading Group



You are invited to join the 2017 African American History Month Reading

Group. Over the course of February 2017, we will read and discuss Ta-Nehisi

Coates=E2=80=99 Between the World and Me, a landmark work that examines Coa=
tes=E2=80=99
experiences and contemporary black life in the context of American history.
Students of all backgrounds and interests are warmly invited. In joining
the group, you will receive a copy of the book and commit to three
hour-long discussions over the course of the month: Feb. 7, 14, and 21, all
Tuesdays, from 4:10 p.m. =E2=80=94 5:10 p.m. To register your interest, ple=
ase
email Dr. Jonathan Hancock at hancockj@hendrix.edu by Friday, Dec. 2, with
a brief paragraph explaining why you would like to join the group.

Pickering Foreign Affairs Fellowship Program



The Thomas R. Pickering Fellowship Program is designed to attract
outstanding college students from all ethnic, racial and social backgrounds
who demonstrate strong leadership and academic excellence, possess a
passion for public service, and have an interest in pursuing a foreign
service career with the U.S. Department of State. This competitive
fellowship provides undergraduate and graduate students with financial
support (up to $37,500 annually), mentoring and professional development to
prepare them academically and professionally for this rewarding career
path. Women, members of minority groups historically underrepresented in
the foreign service, and students with financial need are encouraged to
apply. More information is available online <http://www.twc.edu/pickering>.
The application deadline is January 13, 2017. Interested students should
begin work on their application as soon as possible to ensure all required
components are submitted and received well before this deadline. Email
gess@hendrix.edu to arrange an appointment to begin this process.
